<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">The Beatles</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>The Beatles</b> were an English <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> band, formed in <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> in 1960. With members <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr" title="Ringo Starr">Ringo Starr</a>, they became widely regarded as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_influence_on_popular_culture" title="The Beatles' influence on popular culture">the foremost and most influential act</a> of the rock era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Rooted in <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">skiffle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beat_music" title="Beat music">beat</a>, and 1950s <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a>, the Beatles later experimented with several <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">musical styles</a>, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> <a href="/wiki/Ballad" title="Ballad">ballads</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_India" title="Music of India">Indian music</a> to <a href="/wiki/Psychedelic_music" title="Psychedelic music">psychedelia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a>, often incorporating <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical</a> elements and unconventional <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_recording_technology" title="The Beatles' recording technology">recording techniques</a> in innovative ways. In the early 1960s, their enormous popularity first emerged as "<a href="/wiki/Beatlemania" title="Beatlemania">Beatlemania</a>", but as the group's music grew in sophistication, led by primary songwriters <a href="/wiki/Lennon%E2%80%93McCartney" title="Lennon–McCartney">Lennon and McCartney</a>, they came to be perceived as an embodiment of the ideals shared by the <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">counterculture of the 1960s</a>.</p>
<p>The Beatles built their reputation playing clubs in Liverpool and <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> over a three-year period from 1960, with <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Sutcliffe" title="Stuart Sutcliffe">Stuart Sutcliffe</a> initially serving as bass player. The core of Lennon, McCartney and Harrison went through a succession of drummers, including <a href="/wiki/Pete_Best" title="Pete Best">Pete Best</a>, before asking Starr to join them. Manager <a href="/wiki/Brian_Epstein" title="Brian Epstein">Brian Epstein</a> moulded them into a professional act, and producer <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a> guided and developed their recordings, greatly expanding their popularity in the United Kingdom after their first hit, "<a href="/wiki/Love_Me_Do" title="Love Me Do">Love Me Do</a>", in late 1962. They acquired the nickname "the Fab Four" as Beatlemania grew in Britain the next year, and by early 1964 became international stars, leading the "<a href="/wiki/British_Invasion" title="British Invasion">British Invasion</a>" of the United States pop market. From 1965 onwards, the Beatles produced increasingly innovative recordings, including the albums <i><a href="/wiki/Rubber_Soul" title="Rubber Soul">Rubber Soul</a></i> (1965), <i><a href="/wiki/Revolver_(Beatles_album)" title="Revolver (Beatles album)">Revolver</a></i> (1966), <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> (1967), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)" title="The Beatles (album)">The Beatles</a></i> (commonly known as the White Album, 1968) and <i><a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road" title="Abbey Road">Abbey Road</a></i> (1969). After <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_break-up" title="The Beatles' break-up">their break-up</a> in 1970, they each enjoyed successful musical careers of varying lengths. McCartney and Starr, the surviving members, remain musically active. Lennon was <a href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon" title="Death of John Lennon">shot and killed</a> in December 1980, and Harrison died of lung cancer in November 2001.</p>
<p>The Beatles are the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling band</a> in history, with estimated sales of over 600 million records worldwide. They have had more number-one albums on the British charts and sold more singles in the UK than any other act. According to the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>, the Beatles are also the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists_in_the_United_States" title="List of best-selling music artists in the United States">best-selling music artists in the United States</a>, with 178 million certified units. In 2008, the group topped <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> magazine's list of the all-time most successful "Hot 100" artists; as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Beatles&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, they hold the record for <a href="/wiki/List_of_artists_by_number_of_Billboard_Hot_100_number-one_singles" title="List of artists by number of Billboard Hot 100 number-one singles">most number-one hits on the Hot 100</a> chart with twenty. They have received ten <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Score#1970s" title="Academy Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Song Score</a> and fifteen <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Awards" title="Ivor Novello Awards">Ivor Novello Awards</a>. The group was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1988, and all four were inducted individually from 1994 to 2015. They were also collectively included in <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine's compilation of <a href="/wiki/Time_100:_The_Most_Important_People_of_the_Century" title="Time 100: The Most Important People of the Century">the twentieth century's 100 most influential people</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1957.E2.80.931962:_Formation.2C_Hamburg.2C_and_UK_popularity"><span id="Formation"></span> 1957–1962: Formation, Hamburg, and UK popularity</span></h3>
<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks hlist" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;border-spacing:3px;">

<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:The_Beatles_history&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>

<p>In March 1957, <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>, then aged sixteen, formed a <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">skiffle</a> group with several friends from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quarry_Bank_Grammar_School" title="Quarry Bank Grammar School">Quarry Bank school</a>. They briefly called themselves the Blackjacks, before changing their name to <a href="/wiki/The_Quarrymen" title="The Quarrymen">the Quarrymen</a> after discovering that a respected local group was already using the other name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200547.E2.80.9352_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200547.E2.80.9352-2">[2]</a></sup> Fifteen-year-old <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> joined as a rhythm guitarist shortly after he and Lennon met that July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200593.E2.80.9399_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200593.E2.80.9399-3">[3]</a></sup> In February 1958, McCartney invited his friend <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a> to watch the band. The fourteen-year-old auditioned for Lennon, impressing him with his playing, but Lennon initially thought Harrison was too young to join them. After a month of Harrison's persistence, they enlisted him as their lead guitarist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199747_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199747-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199213_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199213-5">[5]</a></sup> By January 1959, Lennon's Quarry Bank friends had left the group, and he began studies at the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_College_of_Art" title="Liverpool College of Art">Liverpool College of Art</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a103_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a103-6">[6]</a></sup> The three guitarists, billing themselves at least three times as Johnny and the Moondogs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199217_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199217-7">[7]</a></sup> were playing <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> whenever they could find a drummer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b742.E2.80.93743_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b742.E2.80.93743-8">[8]</a></sup> Lennon's art school friend <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Sutcliffe" title="Stuart Sutcliffe">Stuart Sutcliffe</a>, who had recently sold one of his paintings and was persuaded to purchase a bass guitar, joined in January 1960, and it was he who suggested changing the band's name to Beatals, as a tribute to <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly" title="Buddy Holly">Buddy Holly</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Crickets" title="The Crickets">the Crickets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199218_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199218-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilliland1969show_27.2C_track_4_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilliland1969show_27.2C_track_4-10">[10]</a></sup> They used the name until May, when they became the Silver Beetles, before undertaking a brief <a href="/wiki/The_Beat_Ballad_Show_Tour" title="The Beat Ballad Show Tour">tour of Scotland</a> as the backing group for pop singer and fellow Liverpudlian <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Gentle" title="Johnny Gentle">Johnny Gentle</a>. By early July, they had changed their name to the Silver Beatles and by the middle of August to the Beatles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199218.E2.80.9322_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199218.E2.80.9322-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Allan_Williams" title="Allan Williams">Allan Williams</a>, the Beatles' unofficial manager, arranged a residency for them in Hamburg, but lacking a full-time drummer they auditioned and hired <a href="/wiki/Pete_Best" title="Pete Best">Pete Best</a> in mid-August 1960. The band, now a five-piece, left four days later, contracted to club owner <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Koschmider" title="Bruno Koschmider">Bruno Koschmider</a> for what would be a 3½-month residency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199221.E2.80.9325_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199221.E2.80.9325-12">[12]</a></sup> Beatles historian <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lewisohn" title="Mark Lewisohn">Mark Lewisohn</a> writes: "They pulled into Hamburg at dusk on 17 August, the time when the <a href="/wiki/Red-light_district" title="Red-light district">red-light area</a> comes to life ... flashing neon lights screamed out the various entertainment on offer, while scantily clad women sat unabashed in shop windows waiting for business opportunities."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199222_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199222-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koschmider had converted a couple of strip clubs in the district into music venues, and he initially placed the Beatles at the <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_Hamburg" title="The Beatles in Hamburg">Indra Club</a>. After closing the Indra due to noise complaints, he moved them to the <a href="/wiki/Kaiserkeller" title="Kaiserkeller">Kaiserkeller</a> in October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199223_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199223-14">[14]</a></sup> When he learned they had been performing at the rival <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Top_Ten_Club" title="Top Ten Club">Top Ten Club</a> in breach of their contract, he gave the band one month's termination notice,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199224.2C_33_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199224.2C_33-15">[15]</a></sup> and reported the underage Harrison, who had obtained permission to stay in Hamburg by lying to the German authorities about his age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould200788_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould200788-16">[16]</a></sup> The authorities arranged for Harrison's deportation in late November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199224_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199224-17">[17]</a></sup> One week later, Koschmider had McCartney and Best arrested for arson after they set fire to a condom in a concrete corridor; the authorities deported them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199224.E2.80.9325_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199224.E2.80.9325-18">[18]</a></sup> Lennon returned to Liverpool in early December, while Sutcliffe remained in Hamburg through late February with his German fiancée <a href="/wiki/Astrid_Kirchherr" title="Astrid Kirchherr">Astrid Kirchherr</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199225_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199225-19">[19]</a></sup> who took the first semi-professional photos of the Beatles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005222.E2.80.93224_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005222.E2.80.93224-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the next two years, the Beatles were resident for periods in Hamburg, where they used <a href="/wiki/Phenmetrazine" title="Phenmetrazine">Preludin</a> both recreationally and to maintain their energy through all-night performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199766.E2.80.9367_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199766.E2.80.9367-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1961, during their second Hamburg engagement, Kirchherr cut Sutcliffe's hair in the "exi" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Existentialist" title="Existentialist">existentialist</a>) style, later adopted by the other Beatles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199232_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199232-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199776_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199776-23">[23]</a></sup> When Sutcliffe decided to leave the band early that year and resume his art studies in Germany, McCartney took up the bass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould200789.2C_94_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould200789.2C_94-24">[24]</a></sup> Producer <a href="/wiki/Bert_Kaempfert" title="Bert Kaempfert">Bert Kaempfert</a> contracted what was now a four-piece group through June 1962, and he used them as <a href="/wiki/Tony_Sheridan" title="Tony Sheridan">Tony Sheridan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Backup_band" title="Backup band">backing band</a> on a series of recordings for <a href="/wiki/Polydor_Records" title="Polydor Records">Polydor Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilliland1969show_27.2C_track_4_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilliland1969show_27.2C_track_4-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005249.E2.80.93251_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005249.E2.80.93251-25">[25]</a></sup> As part of the sessions, the Beatles were signed to Polydor for one year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn2013450_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn2013450-26">[26]</a></sup> Credited to "Tony Sheridan &amp; the Beat Brothers", the single "<a href="/wiki/My_Bonnie" title="My Bonnie">My Bonnie</a>", recorded in June 1961 and released four months later, reached number 32 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Musikmarkt" title="Musikmarkt">Musikmarkt</a></i> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001100_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001100-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the Beatles completed their second Hamburg residency, they enjoyed increasing popularity in Liverpool with the growing <a href="/wiki/Beat_music" title="Beat music">Merseybeat</a> movement. However, they were also growing tired of the monotony of numerous appearances at the same clubs night after night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199233_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199233-28">[28]</a></sup> In November 1961, during one of the group's frequent performances at the <a href="/wiki/The_Cavern_Club" title="The Cavern Club">Cavern Club</a>, they encountered <a href="/wiki/Brian_Epstein" title="Brian Epstein">Brian Epstein</a>, a local record-store owner and music columnist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199784.E2.80.9387_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199784.E2.80.9387-29">[29]</a></sup> He later recalled: "I immediately liked what I heard. They were fresh, and they were honest, and they had what I thought was a sort of presence ... [a] star quality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199234.E2.80.9335_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199234.E2.80.9335-30">[30]</a></sup> Epstein courted the band over the next couple of months, and they appointed him as their manager in January 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199784.E2.80.9388_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199784.E2.80.9388-31">[31]</a></sup> Throughout early and mid-1962, Epstein sought to free the Beatles from their contractual obligations to Bert Kaempfert Productions. He eventually negotiated a one-month-early release from their contract in exchange for one last recording session in Hamburg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinn200810_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinn200810-32">[32]</a></sup> Tragedy greeted them on their return to Germany in April, when a distraught Kirchherr met them at the airport with news of Sutcliffe's death the previous day from what would later be determined to have been a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cerebral_hemorrhage" title="Cerebral hemorrhage">brain hemorrhage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199256_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199256-33">[33]</a></sup> Epstein began negotiations with record labels for a recording contract. In order to secure a UK record contract, Epstein negotiated an early end to the band's contract with Polydor, in exchange for more recordings backing Tony Sheridan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn2013612.2C_629_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn2013612.2C_629-34">[34]</a></sup> After a New Year's Day audition, <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_Decca_audition" title="The Beatles' Decca audition">Decca Records rejected the band</a> with the comment "Guitar groups are on the way out, Mr. Epstein."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200067_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200067-35">[35]</a></sup> However, three months later, producer <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a> signed the Beatles to <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a> label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199256_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199256-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abbey_Rd_Studios.jpg"><img alt="A flight of stone steps leads from an asphalt car park up to the main entrance of a white two-story building. The ground floor has two sash windows, the first floor has three shorter sash windows. Two more windows are visible at basement level. The decorative stonework around the doors and windows is painted grey." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2508" data-file-width="3762" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Abbey_Rd_Studios.jpg/220px-Abbey_Rd_Studios.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Abbey_Rd_Studios.jpg/330px-Abbey_Rd_Studios.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Abbey_Rd_Studios.jpg/440px-Abbey_Rd_Studios.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abbey_Rd_Studios.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Abbey Road Studios main entrance</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Martin's first recording session with the Beatles took place at EMI's <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a> in London on 6 June 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259-36">[36]</a></sup> Martin immediately complained to Epstein about Best's poor drumming and suggested they use a <a href="/wiki/Session_musician" title="Session musician">session drummer</a> in his place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005318.2C_322_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005318.2C_322-37">[37]</a></sup> Already contemplating Best's dismissal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199849.E2.80.9350_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199849.E2.80.9350-38">[38]</a></sup> the Beatles replaced him in mid-August with <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr" title="Ringo Starr">Ringo Starr</a>, who left <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rory_Storm_and_the_Hurricanes" title="Rory Storm and the Hurricanes">Rory Storm and the Hurricanes</a> to join them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259-36">[36]</a></sup> A 4 September session at EMI yielded a recording of "<a href="/wiki/Love_Me_Do" title="Love Me Do">Love Me Do</a>" featuring Starr on drums, but a dissatisfied Martin hired drummer <a href="/wiki/Andy_White_(drummer)" title="Andy White (drummer)">Andy White</a> for the band's third session a week later, which produced recordings of "Love Me Do", "<a href="/wiki/Please_Please_Me_(song)" title="Please Please Me (song)">Please Please Me</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P.S._I_Love_You_(The_Beatles_song)" title="P.S. I Love You (The Beatles song)">P.S. I Love You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259-36">[36]</a></sup> Martin initially selected the Starr version of "Love Me Do" for the band's first single, though subsequent re-pressings featured the White version, with Starr on tambourine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259_36-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259-36">[36]</a></sup> Released in early October, "Love Me Do" peaked at number seventeen on the <i><a href="/wiki/Record_Retailer" title="Record Retailer">Record Retailer</a></i> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259.E2.80.9360_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259.E2.80.9360-39">[39]</a></sup> Their television debut came later that month with a live performance on the regional news programme <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Granada_Reports" title="Granada Reports">People and Places</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199281.2C_355_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199281.2C_355-40">[40]</a></sup> After Martin suggested rerecording "Please Please Me" at a faster tempo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200090_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200090-41">[41]</a></sup> a studio session in late November yielded that recording,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199262.2C_84_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199262.2C_84-42">[42]</a></sup> of which Martin accurately predicted, "You've just made your first No.1."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a875_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a875-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 1962, the Beatles concluded their fifth and final Hamburg residency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199262.2C_86_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199262.2C_86-44">[44]</a></sup> By 1963, they had agreed that all four band members would contribute vocals to their albums – including Starr, despite his restricted vocal range, to validate his standing in the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007191_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007191-45">[45]</a></sup> Lennon and McCartney had established a songwriting partnership, and as the band's success grew, their dominant collaboration limited Harrison's opportunities as a lead vocalist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a494_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a494-46">[46]</a></sup> Epstein, in an effort to maximise the Beatles' commercial potential, encouraged them to adopt a professional approach to performing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007128.2C_133.E2.80.93134_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007128.2C_133.E2.80.93134-47">[47]</a></sup> Lennon recalled him saying, "Look, if you really want to get in these bigger places, you're going to have to change – stop eating on stage, stop swearing, stop smoking ..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200067_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200067-35">[35]</a></sup> Lennon said: "We used to dress how we liked, on and off stage. He'd tell us that jeans were not particularly smart and could we possibly manage to wear proper trousers, but he didn't want us suddenly looking square. He'd let us have our own sense of individuality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200067_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200067-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1963.E2.80.931966:_Beatlemania_and_touring_years">1963–1966: Beatlemania and touring years</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Please_Please_Me_and_With_the_Beatles"><i>Please Please Me</i> and <i>With the Beatles</i></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beatles_logo.svg"><img alt="The words 'The Beatles', rendered with large letters B and T in the second word" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="90" data-file-width="200" height="77" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Beatles_logo.svg/170px-Beatles_logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Beatles_logo.svg/255px-Beatles_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Beatles_logo.svg/340px-Beatles_logo.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beatles_logo.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Their logo was based on an impromptu sketch by instrument retailer and designer Ivor Arbiter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomack200776_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomack200776-48">[48]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 11 February 1963, the Beatles recorded ten songs during a single studio session for their debut LP, <i><a href="/wiki/Please_Please_Me" title="Please Please Me">Please Please Me</a></i>. The album was supplemented by the four tracks already released on their first two singles. Martin originally considered recording the Beatles' debut LP live at the Cavern Club, but after deciding that the building's acoustics were inadequate, he elected to simulate a "live" album with minimal production in "a single marathon session at Abbey Road".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007147_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007147-49">[49]</a></sup> After the moderate success of "Love Me Do", the single "Please Please Me" met with a more emphatic reception. Released in January 1963, two months ahead of the album of the same name, the song reached number one on every chart in London except <i>Record Retailer</i>, where it stalled at number two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199288.2C_351_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199288.2C_351-50">[50]</a></sup> Recalling how the Beatles "rushed to deliver a debut album, bashing out <i>Please Please Me</i> in a day", <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> comments, "Decades after its release, the album still sounds fresh, precisely because of its intense origins."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErlewine2009a_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErlewine2009a-51">[51]</a></sup> Lennon said little thought went into composition at the time; he and McCartney were "just writing songs <i>à la</i> <a href="/wiki/The_Everly_Brothers" title="The Everly Brothers">Everly Brothers</a>, <i>à la</i> Buddy Holly, pop songs with no more thought of them than that – to create a sound. And the words were almost irrelevant."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981129_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981129-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Released in March 1963, the album initiated a run during which eleven of their twelve studio albums released in the United Kingdom through 1970 reached number one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199290.2C_351_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199290.2C_351-53">[53]</a></sup> The band's third single, "<a href="/wiki/From_Me_to_You" title="From Me to You">From Me to You</a>", came out in April and was also a chart-topping hit, starting an almost unbroken string of seventeen British number-one singles for the Beatles, including all but one of the eighteen they released over the next six years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199289.2C_350.E2.80.93351_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199289.2C_350.E2.80.93351-54">[54]</a></sup> Issued in August, the band's fourth single, "<a href="/wiki/She_Loves_You" title="She Loves You">She Loves You</a>", achieved the fastest sales of any record in the UK up to that time, selling three-quarters of a million copies in under four weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007159_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007159-55">[55]</a></sup> It became their first single to sell a million copies, and remained the biggest-selling record in the UK until 1978, when "<a href="/wiki/Mull_of_Kintyre_(song)" title="Mull of Kintyre (song)">Mull of Kintyre</a>", by McCartney's post-Beatles band <a href="/wiki/Wings_(band)" title="Wings (band)">Wings</a>, surpassed it in sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a990_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a990-56">[56]</a></sup> Their commercial success brought increased media exposure, to which the Beatles responded with an irreverent and comical attitude that defied the expectations of pop musicians at the time, inspiring even more interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007166.E2.80.93169_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007166.E2.80.93169-57">[57]</a></sup> The band toured the UK three times in the first half of the year: a four-week tour that began in February, the Beatles's first nationwide, preceded three-week tours in March and May–June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199290.2C_98.E2.80.93105.2C_109.E2.80.93112_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199290.2C_98.E2.80.93105.2C_109.E2.80.93112-58">[58]</a></sup> As their popularity spread, a frenzied adulation of the group took hold. Greeted with riotous enthusiasm by screaming fans, the press dubbed the phenomenon "<a href="/wiki/Beatlemania" title="Beatlemania">Beatlemania</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005444.E2.80.93445_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005444.E2.80.93445-59">[59]</a></sup> Although not billed as tour leaders, the Beatles overshadowed American acts <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Roe" title="Tommy Roe">Tommy Roe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Montez" title="Chris Montez">Chris Montez</a> during the February engagements and assumed top billing "by audience demand", something no British act had previously accomplished while touring with artists from the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199288_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199288-60">[60]</a></sup> A similar situation arose during their May–June <a href="/wiki/Roy_Orbison/The_Beatles_Tour" title="Roy Orbison/The Beatles Tour">tour with Roy Orbison</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199290_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199290-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_and_Lill-Babs_1963.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1436" data-file-width="1844" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/The_Beatles_and_Lill-Babs_1963.jpg/220px-The_Beatles_and_Lill-Babs_1963.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/The_Beatles_and_Lill-Babs_1963.jpg/330px-The_Beatles_and_Lill-Babs_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/The_Beatles_and_Lill-Babs_1963.jpg/440px-The_Beatles_and_Lill-Babs_1963.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_and_Lill-Babs_1963.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McCartney, Harrison, Swedish pop singer <a href="/wiki/Lill-Babs" title="Lill-Babs">Lill-Babs</a> and Lennon on the set of the Swedish television show <i>Drop-In</i>, 30 October 1963<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199886_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199886-62">[62]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In late October, the Beatles began a five-day tour of Sweden, their first time abroad since the final Hamburg engagement of December 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1088_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1088-63">[63]</a></sup> On their return to the UK on 31 October, according to Lewisohn, "several hundred screaming fans" greeted them in heavy rain at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" title="London Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a>. Around 50 to 100 journalists and photographers as well as representatives from the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Television" title="BBC Television">BBC</a> also joined the airport reception, the first of more than 100 such events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199292.E2.80.9393_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199292.E2.80.9393-64">[64]</a></sup> The next day, the band began its fourth tour of Britain within nine months, this one scheduled for six weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992127.E2.80.93133_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992127.E2.80.93133-65">[65]</a></sup> In mid-November, as Beatlemania intensified, police resorted to using high-pressure water hoses to control the crowd before a concert in Plymouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1968184.E2.80.93185_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1968184.E2.80.93185-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Please Please Me</i> maintained the top position on the <i>Record Retailer</i> chart for 30 weeks, only to be displaced by its follow-up, <i><a href="/wiki/With_the_Beatles" title="With the Beatles">With the Beatles</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199290.2C_92.2C_100_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199290.2C_92.2C_100-67">[67]</a></sup> On 22 November EMI released <i>With the Beatles</i> to record advance orders of 270,000 copies, and the LP topped a half-million albums sold in one week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199293_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199293-68">[68]</a></sup> Recorded between July and October, <i>With the Beatles</i> made better use of studio production techniques than its predecessor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007187_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007187-69">[69]</a></sup> It held the top spot for 21 weeks with a chart life of 40 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1161_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1161-70">[70]</a></sup> Erlewine described the LP as "a sequel of the highest order – one that betters the original".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErlewine2009b_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErlewine2009b-71">[71]</a></sup> In a reversal of then standard practice, EMI released the album ahead of the impending single "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Hold_Your_Hand" title="I Want to Hold Your Hand">I Want to Hold Your Hand</a>", with the song excluded to maximise the single's sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007187.E2.80.93188_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007187.E2.80.93188-72">[72]</a></sup> The album caught the attention of music critic <a href="/wiki/William_Mann_(critic)" title="William Mann (critic)">William Mann</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, who suggested that Lennon and McCartney were "the outstanding English composers of 1963".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007187_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007187-69">[69]</a></sup> The newspaper published a series of articles in which Mann offered detailed analyses of the music, lending it respectability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1162_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1162-73">[73]</a></sup> <i>With the Beatles</i> became the second album in UK chart history to sell a million copies, a figure previously reached only by the 1958 <i><a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_(musical)" title="South Pacific (musical)">South Pacific</a></i> soundtrack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b978_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b978-74">[74]</a></sup> When writing the sleeve notes for the album, the band's press officer, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Barrow" title="Tony Barrow">Tony Barrow</a>, used the superlative the "fabulous foursome", which the media widely adopted as "the Fab Four".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a402_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a402-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id=".22British_Invasion.22">"British Invasion"</span></h4>
<p>EMI's American subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a>, hindered the Beatles' releases in the United States for more than a year by initially declining to issue their music, including their first three singles. Concurrent negotiations with the independent US label <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vee-Jay" title="Vee-Jay">Vee-Jay</a> led to the release of some of the songs in 1963, but not all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350-76">[76]</a></sup> Vee-Jay finished preparation for the album <i><a href="/wiki/Introducing..._The_Beatles" title="Introducing... The Beatles">Introducing... The Beatles</a></i>, culled from most of the songs of Parlophone's <i>Please Please Me</i>, but a management shake-up led to the album not being released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[nb 1]</a></sup> Then when it surfaced that the label did not report royalties on their sales, the licence Vee-Jay signed with EMI was voided.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpizer200440_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpizer200440-79">[78]</a></sup> A new licence was granted to the <a href="/wiki/Swan_Records" title="Swan Records">Swan</a> label for the single "She Loves You", but legal issues with royalties and publishing rights proved an obstacle to the successful marketing of the group in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a225.E2.80.93226.2C_228.2C_1118.E2.80.931122_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a225.E2.80.93226.2C_228.2C_1118.E2.80.931122-80">[79]</a></sup> American chart success began after Epstein arranged for a $40,000 US marketing campaign and secured the support of disc jockey Carrol James, who first played the band's records in mid-December 1963. Late that same month, the Beatles were introduced in the Tidewater area of Virginia by Gene Loving of radio station <a href="/wiki/WGH_(AM)" title="WGH (AM)">WGH</a>, accompanied by a full marketing campaign, including Beatles shirt giveaways. Within days, almost every other song played on the station was a Beatles recording. It was not until the end of first week of January 1964 that their records were played in New York City (also accompanied by a major marketing campaign and with similar play frequency), and then the rest of the country, initiating their music's spread across US radio. This caused an increase in demand, leading Capitol to rush-release "I Want to Hold Your Hand" later that month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001206_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001206-81">[80]</a></sup> Issued on 26 December 1963, with the band's previously scheduled debut there just weeks away, "I Want to Hold Your Hand" sold a million copies, becoming a number-one hit in the US by mid-January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992136.2C_350_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992136.2C_350-82">[81]</a></sup> In its wake, Vee-Jay released <i>Introducing... The Beatles</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpizer200496_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpizer200496-83">[82]</a></sup> to go along with Capitol's debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Beatles!" title="Meet the Beatles!">Meet the Beatles!</a></i>, while Swan reactivated production of "She Loves You".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1968218_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1968218-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_in_America.JPG"><img alt="A black and white image of four men are standing in front of a crowd of people at the bottom of an aeroplane staircase." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2526" data-file-width="3578" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/220px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/330px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/440px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_in_America.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Beatles arrive at John F. Kennedy International Airport, 7 February 1964</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 7 February 1964, the Beatles left the United Kingdom with an estimated 4,000 fans gathered at Heathrow, waving and screaming as the aircraft took off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005457_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005457-85">[84]</a></sup> Upon landing at New York's <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy Airport</a>, an uproarious crowd estimated at 3,000 greeted them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005459_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005459-86">[85]</a></sup> They gave their first live US television performance two days later on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ed_Sullivan_Show" title="The Ed Sullivan Show">The Ed Sullivan Show</a></i>, watched by approximately 73 million viewers in over 23 million households,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992137_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992137-87">[86]</a></sup> or 34 per cent of the American population. Biographer Jonathan Gould writes that, according to the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_ratings" title="Nielsen ratings">Nielsen</a> rating service, it was "the largest audience that had ever been recorded for an American television <span lang="en-US">program</span>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould20073_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould20073-88">[87]</a></sup> The next morning, the Beatles awoke to a negative critical consensus in the US,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005473.E2.80.93474_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005473.E2.80.93474-89">[88]</a></sup> but a day later their first US concert saw Beatlemania erupt at <a href="/wiki/Washington_Coliseum" title="Washington Coliseum">Washington Coliseum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1134.E2.80.931135_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1134.E2.80.931135-90">[89]</a></sup> Back in New York the following day, the Beatles met with another strong reception during two shows at <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Hall" title="Carnegie Hall">Carnegie Hall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992137_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992137-87">[86]</a></sup> The band then flew to Florida and appeared on the weekly <i>Ed Sullivan Show</i> a second time, before another 70 million viewers, before returning to the UK on 22 February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992137.2C_146.E2.80.93147_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992137.2C_146.E2.80.93147-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="A_Hard_Day.27s_Night"><i>A Hard Day's Night</i></span></h4>
<p>Capitol Records' lack of interest throughout 1963 had not gone unnoticed, and a competitor, <a href="/wiki/United_Artists_Records" title="United Artists Records">United Artists Records</a>, encouraged <a href="/wiki/United_Artists" title="United Artists">their film division</a> to offer the group a three-motion-picture deal, primarily for the commercial potential of the soundtracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a483.E2.80.93484_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a483.E2.80.93484-92">[91]</a></sup> Directed by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lester" title="Richard Lester">Richard Lester</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Hard_Day%27s_Night_(film)" title="A Hard Day's Night (film)">A Hard Day's Night</a></i> involved the band for six weeks in March–April 1964 as they played themselves in a <a href="/wiki/Mockumentary" title="Mockumentary">mock-documentary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007230.E2.80.93232_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007230.E2.80.93232-93">[92]</a></sup> The film premiered in London and New York in July and August, respectively, and was an international success, with some critics drawing comparison with the <a href="/wiki/Marx_Brothers" title="Marx Brothers">Marx Brothers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a489.E2.80.93490_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a489.E2.80.93490-94">[93]</a></sup> According to Erlewine, the accompanying soundtrack album, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Hard_Day%27s_Night_(album)" title="A Hard Day's Night (album)">A Hard Day's Night</a></i>, saw them "truly coming into their own as a band. All of the disparate influences on their first two albums had coalesced into a bright, joyous, original sound, filled with ringing guitars and irresistible melodies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErlewine2009c_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErlewine2009c-95">[94]</a></sup> That "ringing guitar" sound was primarily the product of Harrison's <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker_360/12" title="Rickenbacker 360/12">12-string electric Rickenbacker</a>, a prototype given to him by the manufacturer, which made its debut on the record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007286.E2.80.93287_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007286.E2.80.93287-96">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[nb 2]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the week of 4 April 1964, the Beatles held twelve positions on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> singles chart, including the top five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992138_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992138-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[nb 3]</a></sup> Their popularity generated unprecedented interest in British music, and a number of other UK acts subsequently made their own American debuts, successfully touring over the next three years in what was termed the <a href="/wiki/British_Invasion" title="British Invasion">British Invasion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould20079.2C_250.2C_285_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould20079.2C_250.2C_285-101">[98]</a></sup> Their hairstyle, unusually long for the era and mocked by many adults,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilliland1969show_27.2C_track_4_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilliland1969show_27.2C_track_4-10">[10]</a></sup> became an emblem of rebellion to the burgeoning youth culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007345_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007345-102">[99]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul,_George_%26_John.png"><img alt="Paul McCartney, George Harrison, and John Lennon playing guitars and wearing matching grey suits." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="329" data-file-width="500" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Paul%2C_George_%26_John.png/220px-Paul%2C_George_%26_John.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Paul%2C_George_%26_John.png/330px-Paul%2C_George_%26_John.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Paul%2C_George_%26_John.png/440px-Paul%2C_George_%26_John.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul,_George_%26_John.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McCartney, Harrison and Lennon perform on Dutch television in 1964</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Touring internationally in June and July, the Beatles staged 37 shows over 27 days in Denmark, the Netherlands, Hong Kong, Australia and New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992161.E2.80.93165_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992161.E2.80.93165-103">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[nb 4]</a></sup> In August they returned to the US, with a 30-concert tour of 23 cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007249_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007249-106">[102]</a></sup> Generating intense interest once again, the month-long tour attracted between 10,000 and 20,000 fans to each 30-minute performance in cities from San Francisco to New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007249_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007249-106">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August, journalist <a href="/wiki/Al_Aronowitz" title="Al Aronowitz">Al Aronowitz</a> arranged for the Beatles to meet <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007252_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007252-107">[103]</a></sup> Visiting the band in their New York hotel suite, Dylan introduced them to <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997185_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997185-108">[104]</a></sup> Gould points out the musical and cultural significance of this meeting, before which the musicians' respective fanbases were "perceived as inhabiting two separate subcultural worlds": Dylan's audience of "college kids with artistic or intellectual leanings, a dawning political and social idealism, and a mildly bohemian style" contrasted with their fans, "veritable '<a href="/wiki/Teenybopper" title="Teenybopper">teenyboppers</a>' – kids in high school or grade school whose lives were totally wrapped up in the commercialised popular culture of television, radio, pop records, fan magazines, and teen fashion. They were seen as idolaters, not idealists."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007252.E2.80.93253_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007252.E2.80.93253-109">[105]</a></sup> Within six months of the meeting, Gould writes, "Lennon would be making records on which he openly imitated Dylan's nasal drone, brittle strum, and introspective vocal persona".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007252.E2.80.93253_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007252.E2.80.93253-109">[105]</a></sup> Within a year, "the distinctions between the folk and rock audiences would have nearly evaporated [and the group's] audience ... [was] showing signs of growing up."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007252.E2.80.93253_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007252.E2.80.93253-109">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[nb 5]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beatles_for_Sale.2C_Help.21_and_Rubber_Soul"><i>Beatles for Sale</i>, <i>Help!</i> and <i>Rubber Soul</i></span></h4>
<p>According to Gould, <i><a href="/wiki/Beatles_for_Sale" title="Beatles for Sale">Beatles for Sale</a></i>, the Beatles' fourth studio LP, evidenced a growing conflict between the commercial pressures of their global success and their creative ambitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007255.E2.80.9356_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007255.E2.80.9356-112">[107]</a></sup> They had intended the album, recorded between August and October 1964,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992167.E2.80.93176_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992167.E2.80.93176-113">[108]</a></sup> to continue the format established by <i>A Hard Day's Night</i> which, unlike the group's first two LPs, contained only original songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007255.E2.80.93256_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007255.E2.80.93256-114">[109]</a></sup> The band had nearly exhausted their backlog of songs on the previous album, however, and given the challenges constant international touring posed to their songwriting efforts, Lennon admitted, "Material's becoming a hell of a problem".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007256_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007256-115">[110]</a></sup> As a result, six covers from their extensive repertoire were chosen to complete the album. Released in early December, its eight original compositions stood out, demonstrating the growing maturity of the <a href="/wiki/Lennon%E2%80%93McCartney" title="Lennon–McCartney">Lennon–McCartney</a> songwriting partnership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007255.E2.80.93256_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007255.E2.80.93256-114">[109]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beatles_ad_1965_just_the_beatles_crop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="839" data-file-width="1156" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Beatles_ad_1965_just_the_beatles_crop.jpg/220px-Beatles_ad_1965_just_the_beatles_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Beatles_ad_1965_just_the_beatles_crop.jpg/330px-Beatles_ad_1965_just_the_beatles_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Beatles_ad_1965_just_the_beatles_crop.jpg/440px-Beatles_ad_1965_just_the_beatles_crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beatles_ad_1965_just_the_beatles_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Together in 1965, celebrating a Grammy win</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In early 1965, while they were his guests for dinner, Lennon and Harrison's dentist secretly added <a href="/wiki/Lysergic_acid_diethylamide" title="Lysergic acid diethylamide">LSD</a> to their coffee. Lennon described the experience: "It was just terrifying, but it was fantastic. I was pretty stunned for a month or two."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007316_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007316-116">[111]</a></sup> He and Harrison subsequently became regular users of the drug, joined by Starr on at least one occasion. McCartney was initially reluctant to try it, but eventually did so in late 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007317_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007317-117">[112]</a></sup> He became the first Beatle to discuss LSD publicly, declaring in a magazine interview that "it opened my eyes" and "made me a better, more honest, more tolerant member of society".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002228_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002228-118">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Controversy erupted in June 1965 when <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> appointed all four Beatles <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Members of the Order of the British Empire (MBE)</a> after Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> nominated them for the award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005556_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005556-119">[114]</a></sup> In protest – the honour was at that time primarily bestowed upon military veterans and civic leaders – some conservative MBE recipients returned their own insignia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005557_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005557-120">[115]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TrailerUSHelp.jpg"><img alt="The Beatles performing music in a field. In the foreground, the drums are played by Starr (only the top of his head is visible). Beyond him, the other three stand in a column with their guitars. In the rear, Harrison, head down, strikes a chord. In the front, Lennon smiles and gives a little wave toward camera, holding his pick. Between them, McCartney is jocularly about to choke Lennon." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="641" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/TrailerUSHelp.jpg/220px-TrailerUSHelp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/TrailerUSHelp.jpg/330px-TrailerUSHelp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/TrailerUSHelp.jpg/440px-TrailerUSHelp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TrailerUSHelp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The US trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/Help!_(film)" title="Help! (film)">Help!</a></i> with (from the rear) Harrison, McCartney, Lennon and (largely obscured) Starr</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Released in July, the Beatles' second film, <i><a href="/wiki/Help!_(film)" title="Help! (film)">Help!</a></i>, was again directed by Lester. Described as "mainly a relentless spoof of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_series)" title="James Bond (film series)">Bond</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007275_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007275-121">[116]</a></sup> it inspired a mixed response among both reviewers and the band. McCartney said: "<i>Help!</i> was great but it wasn't our film – we were sort of guest stars. It was fun, but basically, as an idea for a film, it was a bit wrong."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007274_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007274-122">[117]</a></sup> The soundtrack was dominated by Lennon, who wrote and sang lead on most of its songs, including the two singles: "<a href="/wiki/Help!_(song)" title="Help! (song)">Help!</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Ticket_to_Ride" title="Ticket to Ride">Ticket to Ride</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007276.E2.80.93277_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007276.E2.80.93277-123">[118]</a></sup> The accompanying album, the group's fifth studio LP, contained all original material save for two covers, "<a href="/wiki/Act_Naturally" title="Act Naturally">Act Naturally</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dizzy,_Miss_Lizzy" title="Dizzy, Miss Lizzy">Dizzy Miss Lizzy</a>"; they were the last covers the band would include on an album, with the exception of <i><a href="/wiki/Let_It_Be" title="Let It Be">Let It Be</a>'s</i> brief rendition of the traditional Liverpool folk song "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maggie_May_(traditional_song)" title="Maggie May (traditional song)">Maggie Mae</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007276.E2.80.93280_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007276.E2.80.93280-124">[119]</a></sup> The band expanded their use of vocal overdubs on <i><a href="/wiki/Help!_(album)" title="Help! (album)">Help!</a></i> and incorporated classical instruments into some arrangements, including a string quartet on the pop ballad "<a href="/wiki/Yesterday_(Beatles_song)" title="Yesterday (Beatles song)">Yesterday</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007290.E2.80.93292_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007290.E2.80.93292-125">[120]</a></sup> Composed by McCartney, "Yesterday" would inspire the most recorded cover versions of any song ever written.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuinness_World_Records_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuinness_World_Records-126">[121]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beatles_press_conference_1965.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="585" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Beatles_press_conference_1965.jpg/220px-Beatles_press_conference_1965.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Beatles_press_conference_1965.jpg/330px-Beatles_press_conference_1965.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Beatles_press_conference_1965.jpg/440px-Beatles_press_conference_1965.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beatles_press_conference_1965.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Beatles at a press conference in <a href="/wiki/Bloomington,_Minnesota" title="Bloomington, Minnesota">Bloomington, Minnesota</a>, in August 1965</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The group's third US tour opened with a performance before a world-record crowd of 55,600 at New York's <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a> on 15 August 1965 – "perhaps the most famous of all Beatles' concerts", in Lewisohn's description.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992181_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992181-127">[122]</a></sup> A further nine successful concerts followed in other American cities. At a show in Atlanta, the Beatles gave one of the first live performances ever to make use of a <a href="/wiki/Foldback_(sound_engineering)" title="Foldback (sound engineering)">foldback</a> system of on-stage monitor speakers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEmerson2009_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEmerson2009-128">[123]</a></sup> Towards the end of the tour, they met with <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, a foundational musical influence on the band, who invited them to his home in <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills,_California" title="Beverly Hills, California">Beverly Hills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a882.E2.80.93883_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a882.E2.80.93883-129">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007283.E2.80.93284_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007283.E2.80.93284-130">[125]</a></sup> September saw the launch of an American Saturday-morning cartoon series, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(TV_series)" title="The Beatles (TV series)">The Beatles</a></i>, that echoed <i>A Hard Day's Night</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> slapstick antics over its two-year original run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeil199682_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeil199682-131">[126]</a></sup> The series was a historical milestone as the first weekly television series to feature animated versions of real, living people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Animators_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Animators-132">[127]</a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
