The releases were commercially successful and the television series was viewed by an estimated 400 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a111.E2.80.93112_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a111.E2.80.93112-290">[283]</a></sup> In 1999, to coincide with the re-release of the 1968 film <i>Yellow Submarine</i>, a new soundtrack compilation CD/LP, <i><a href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_Songtrack" title="Yellow Submarine Songtrack">Yellow Submarine Songtrack</a></i>, was issued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009342_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009342-291">[284]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span></h4>
<p>The Beatles' <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_(The_Beatles_album)" title="1 (The Beatles album)">1</a></i>, a compilation album of the band's British and American number-one hits, was released on 13 November 2000. It became the fastest-selling album of all time, with 3.6 million sold in its first week<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECNN.com2000_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECNN.com2000-292">[285]</a></sup> and 13 million within a month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould20079_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould20079-293">[286]</a></sup> It topped albums charts in at least 28 countries, including the UK and US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006204_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006204-294">[287]</a></sup> As of April 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Beatles&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the compilation had sold 31 million copies globally,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2009_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2009-295">[288]</a></sup> and was the best-selling album of the decade in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevine2009_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevine2009-296">[289]</a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison died from <a href="/wiki/Metastasis" title="Metastasis">metastatic</a> lung cancer in November 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Smoking_Gun2001_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Smoking_Gun2001-297">[290]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_Online2001_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_Online2001-298">[291]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003119_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003119-299">[292]</a></sup> McCartney and Starr were among the musicians who performed at the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_George" title="Concert for George">Concert for George</a>, organised by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> and Harrison's widow, <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Harrison" title="Olivia Harrison">Olivia</a>. The tribute event took place at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> on the first anniversary of Harrison's death. In addition to songs he composed for the group and during his solo career, the concert included a celebration of <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a>, which had significantly influenced Harrison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139-300">[293]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, <i><a href="/wiki/Let_It_Be..._Naked" title="Let It Be... Naked">Let It Be... Naked</a></i>, a reconceived version of the <i>Let It Be</i> album, with McCartney supervising production, was released. One of the main differences with the Spector-produced version was the omission of the original string arrangements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHurwitz2004_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHurwitz2004-301">[294]</a></sup> It was a top ten hit in both Britain and America. The US album configurations from 1964 to 1965 were released as box sets in 2004 and 2006 – <i><a href="/wiki/The_Capitol_Albums,_Volume_1" title="The Capitol Albums, Volume 1">The Capitol Albums, Volume 1</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Capitol_Albums,_Volume_2" title="The Capitol Albums, Volume 2">Volume 2</a></i> included both stereo and mono versions based on the mixes that were prepared for vinyl at the time of the music's original American release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomack2007100_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomack2007100-302">[295]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a soundtrack for <a href="/wiki/Cirque_du_Soleil" title="Cirque du Soleil">Cirque du Soleil</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">Las Vegas</a> Beatles stage revue, <i><a href="/wiki/Love_(Cirque_du_Soleil)" title="Love (Cirque du Soleil)">Love</a></i>, George Martin and his son <a href="/wiki/Giles_Martin" title="Giles Martin">Giles</a> remixed and <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">blended</a> 130 of the band's recordings to create what Martin called "a way of re-living the whole Beatles musical lifespan in a very condensed period".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENME2006_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENME2006-303">[296]</a></sup> The show premiered in June 2006, and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Love_(The_Beatles_album)" title="Love (The Beatles album)">Love</a></i> album was released that November when McCartney discussed his hope that "<a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Light" title="Carnival of Light">Carnival of Light</a>", a fourteen-minute experimental recording made at Abbey Road in 1967, would receive an official release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollett-White2008_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollett-White2008-304">[297]</a></sup> A rare live performance involving two ex-Beatles took place in April 2009 at a benefit concert organised by McCartney at New York's <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a>, where he was joined by Starr for three songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELustig2009_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELustig2009-305">[298]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg"><img alt="A photograph of two older men, one using a microphone, in front of a large electronic display" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="528" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg/220px-Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg/330px-Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg/440px-Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr and McCartney introduced the video game <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles:_Rock_Band" title="The Beatles: Rock Band">The Beatles: Rock Band</a></i> at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo">E3</a> convention.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 9 September 2009, the Beatles' entire back catalogue was reissued following an extensive digital remastering process that lasted four years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEMI7_April_2009_282-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEMI7_April_2009-282">[275]</a></sup> Stereo editions of all twelve original UK studio albums, along with <i>Magical Mystery Tour</i> and the <i>Past Masters</i> compilation, were released on compact disc both individually and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Stereo_Box_Set" title="The Beatles Stereo Box Set">as a box set</a>. Comparing the new releases with the 1987 CDs, which had been widely criticised for their lack of clarity and dynamism, <i><a href="/wiki/Mojo_(magazine)" title="Mojo (magazine)">Mojo</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Danny Eccleston wrote, "the remastered vocals are purer, more natural-sounding and give the illusion of sitting slightly higher in the mix."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEccleston2009_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEccleston2009-306">[299]</a></sup> A second collection, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_Mono" title="The Beatles in Mono">The Beatles in Mono</a></i>, included remastered versions of every Beatles album released in true mono along with the original 1965 stereo mixes of <i>Help!</i> and <i>Rubber Soul</i> (which Martin had remixed for the 1987 editions).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollett-White2009_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollett-White2009-307">[300]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles:_Rock_Band" title="The Beatles: Rock Band">The Beatles: Rock Band</a></i>, a music video game in the <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band" title="Rock Band">Rock Band</a></i> series, was issued on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGross2009_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGross2009-308">[301]</a></sup> In December 2009, the band's catalogue was officially released in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_Lossless_Audio_Codec" title="Free Lossless Audio Codec">FLAC</a> and MP3 format in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Stereo_Box_Set#Limited_edition_USB_flash_drive" title="The Beatles Stereo Box Set">a limited edition of 30,000 USB flash drives</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartens2009_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartens2009-309">[302]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span></h4>
<p>Owing to a long-running royalty disagreement, the Beatles were among the last major artists to sign deals with online music services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELa_Monica2005_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELa_Monica2005-310">[303]</a></sup> Residual disagreement emanating from <a href="/wiki/Apple_Corps_v_Apple_Computer" title="Apple Corps v Apple Computer">Apple Corps' dispute with Apple, Inc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>' owners, over the use of the name "Apple" was also partly responsible for the delay, although in 2008, McCartney stated that the main obstacle to making the Beatles' catalogue available online was that EMI "want[s] something we're not prepared to give them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaplan2008_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaplan2008-311">[304]</a></sup> In 2010, the official canon of thirteen Beatles studio albums, <i>Past Masters</i>, and the <i>Red</i> and <i>Blue</i> greatest-hits albums were made available on iTunes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAswad2010_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAswad2010-312">[305]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, EMI's recorded music operations were sold to <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a>. In order for Universal Music to acquire EMI, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antitrust" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> reasons, forced EMI to spin off assets including Parlophone. Universal was allowed to keep the Beatles' recorded music catalogue, managed by <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a> under its <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Music_Group" title="Capitol Music Group">Capitol Music Group</a> division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[306]</a></sup> Also in 2012, the entire original Beatles album catalogue was reissued on vinyl, available either individually or as a box set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2012_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2012-314">[307]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, a second volume of BBC recordings entitled <i><a href="/wiki/On_Air_%E2%80%93_Live_at_the_BBC_Volume_2" title="On Air – Live at the BBC Volume 2">On Air – Live at the BBC Volume 2</a></i> was released. December of that year saw the release of another 59 Beatles recordings on iTunes. The set, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Bootleg_Recordings_1963" title="The Beatles Bootleg Recordings 1963">The Beatles Bootleg Recordings 1963</a></i>, had the opportunity to gain a 70-year copyright extension conditional on the songs being published at least once before the end of 2013. Apple Records released the recordings on 17 December to prevent them from going into the public domain and had them taken down from iTunes later that same day. Fan reactions to the release were mixed, with one blogger saying "the hardcore Beatles collectors who are trying to obtain everything will already have these."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[308]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[309]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 January 2014, Paul McCartney and Ringo Starr performed McCartney's "<a href="/wiki/Queenie_Eye" title="Queenie Eye">Queenie Eye</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> at the <a href="/wiki/56th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="56th Annual Grammy Awards">56th Annual Grammy Awards</a>, held at the <a href="/wiki/Staples_Center" title="Staples Center">Staples Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[310]</a></sup> The following day, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_That_Changed_America:_A_Grammy_Salute_to_The_Beatles" title="The Night That Changed America: A Grammy Salute to The Beatles">The Night That Changed America: A Grammy Salute to The Beatles</a></i> television special was taped in the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Convention_Center" title="Los Angeles Convention Center">Los Angeles Convention Center</a>'s West Hall. It aired on 9 February, the exact date of – and at the same time, and on the same network as – the original broadcast of the Beatles' first US television appearance on <i>The Ed Sullivan Show</i>, 50 years earlier. The special included performances of Beatles songs by current artists as well as by McCartney and Starr, archival footage, and Paul and Ringo being interviewed by <a href="/wiki/David_Letterman" title="David Letterman">David Letterman</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sullivan_Theater" title="Ed Sullivan Theater">Ed Sullivan Theater</a>, site of <i>The Ed Sullivan Show</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[311]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[312]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2015 the Beatles released their catalogue for streaming on various streaming music services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[313]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style_and_development">Musical style and development</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Lennon%E2%80%93McCartney" title="Lennon–McCartney">Lennon–McCartney</a></div>
<p>In <i>Icons of Rock: An Encyclopedia of the Legends Who Changed Music Forever</i>, Scott Schinder and Andy Schwartz describe the Beatles' musical evolution:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>In their initial incarnation as cheerful, wisecracking moptops, the Fab Four revolutionised the sound, style, and attitude of popular music and opened rock and roll's doors to a tidal wave of British rock acts. Their initial impact would have been enough to establish the Beatles as one of their era's most influential cultural forces, but they didn't stop there. Although their initial style was a highly original, irresistibly catchy synthesis of early American rock and roll and R&amp;B, the Beatles spent the rest of the 1960s expanding rock's stylistic frontiers, consistently staking out new musical territory on each release. The band's increasingly sophisticated experimentation encompassed a variety of genres, including folk-rock, country, psychedelia, and baroque pop, without sacrificing the effortless mass appeal of their early work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchinderSchwartz2007160_321-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchinderSchwartz2007160-321">[314]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In <i>The Beatles as Musicians</i>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Everett_(musicologist)" title="Walter Everett (musicologist)">Walter Everett</a> describes Lennon and McCartney's contrasting motivations and approaches to composition: "McCartney may be said to have constantly developed – as a means to entertain – a focused musical talent with an ear for counterpoint and other aspects of craft in the demonstration of a universally agreed-upon common language that he did much to enrich. Conversely, Lennon's mature music is best appreciated as the daring product of a largely unconscious, searching but undisciplined artistic sensibility."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett19999_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett19999-322">[315]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ian MacDonald describes McCartney as "a natural melodist – a creator of tunes capable of existing apart from their harmony". His melody lines are characterised as primarily "vertical", employing wide, <a href="/wiki/Consonance_and_dissonance" title="Consonance and dissonance">consonant</a> intervals which express his "extrovert energy and optimism". Conversely, Lennon's "sedentary, ironic personality" is reflected in a "horizontal" approach featuring minimal, dissonant intervals and repetitive melodies which rely on their harmonic accompaniment for interest: "Basically a realist, he instinctively kept his melodies close to the rhythms and cadences of speech, colouring his lyrics with bluesy tone and harmony rather than creating tunes that made striking shapes of their own."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald200512_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald200512-323">[316]</a></sup> MacDonald praises Harrison's lead guitar work for the role his "characterful lines and textural colourings" play in supporting Lennon and McCartney's parts, and describes Starr as "the father of modern pop/rock drumming".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005382.E2.80.93383_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005382.E2.80.93383-324">[317]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h3>
<p>The band's earliest influences include <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Perkins" title="Carl Perkins">Carl Perkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Richard" title="Little Richard">Little Richard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry" title="Chuck Berry">Chuck Berry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a140.2C_660.2C_856.E2.80.93858.2C_881_325-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a140.2C_660.2C_856.E2.80.93858.2C_881-325">[318]</a></sup> During the Beatles' co-residency with Little Richard at the <a href="/wiki/Star-Club" title="Star-Club">Star-Club</a> in Hamburg, from April to May 1962, he advised them on the proper technique for performing his songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a660_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a660-326">[319]</a></sup> Of Presley, Lennon said, "Nothing really affected me until I heard Elvis. If there hadn't been Elvis, there would not have been the Beatles."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a881_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a881-327">[320]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other early influences include <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly" title="Buddy Holly">Buddy Holly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Cochran" title="Eddie Cochran">Eddie Cochran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Orbison" title="Roy Orbison">Roy Orbison</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a289.2C_526.2C_830_328-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a289.2C_526.2C_830-328">[321]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Everly_Brothers" title="The Everly Brothers">the Everly Brothers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005111.2C_123.2C_131.2C_133_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005111.2C_123.2C_131.2C_133-329">[322]</a></sup> The Beatles continued to absorb influences long after their initial success, often finding new musical and lyrical avenues by listening to their contemporaries, including <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">the Who</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Zappa" title="Frank Zappa">Frank Zappa</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Lovin%27_Spoonful" title="The Lovin' Spoonful">the Lovin' Spoonful</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Byrds" title="The Byrds">the Byrds</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys" title="The Beach Boys">the Beach Boys</a>, whose 1966 album <i><a href="/wiki/Pet_Sounds" title="Pet Sounds">Pet Sounds</a></i> amazed and inspired McCartney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a99.2C_217.2C_357.2C_1195_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a99.2C_217.2C_357.2C_1195-330">[323]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007333.E2.80.93335.2C_359_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007333.E2.80.93335.2C_359-331">[324]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006147.2C_150.2C_162.2C_169_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006147.2C_150.2C_162.2C_169-332">[325]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[326]</a></sup> Referring to the Beach Boys' creative leader, Martin later stated: "No one made a greater impact on the Beatles than Brian [Wilson]."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGranata200317_334-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGranata200317-334">[327]</a></sup> Ravi Shankar, with whom Harrison studied for six weeks in India in late 1966, had a significant effect on his musical development during the band's later years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006147.2C_165.2C_177_335-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006147.2C_165.2C_177-335">[328]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genres">Genres</span></h3>
<p>Originating as a skiffle group, the Beatles quickly embraced 1950s rock and roll and helped pioneer the Merseybeat genre,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[329]</a></sup> and their repertoire ultimately expanded to include a broad variety of pop music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould200730.E2.80.9332.2C_100.E2.80.93107_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould200730.E2.80.9332.2C_100.E2.80.93107-337">[330]</a></sup> Reflecting the range of styles they explored, Lennon said of <i>Beatles for Sale</i>, "You could call our new one a Beatles country-and-western LP",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007255_338-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007255-338">[331]</a></sup> while Gould credits <i>Rubber Soul</i> as "the instrument by which legions of folk-music enthusiasts were coaxed into the camp of pop".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007296_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007296-339">[332]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guitarras_de_McCartney_y_Harrison.jpg"><img alt="Two electric guitars, a light brown violin-shaped bass and a darker brown guitar, rest against a Vox amplifier." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="853" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Guitarras_de_McCartney_y_Harrison.jpg/170px-Guitarras_de_McCartney_y_Harrison.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Guitarras_de_McCartney_y_Harrison.jpg/255px-Guitarras_de_McCartney_y_Harrison.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Guitarras_de_McCartney_y_Harrison.jpg/340px-Guitarras_de_McCartney_y_Harrison.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guitarras_de_McCartney_y_Harrison.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6fner_500/1" title="Höfner 500/1">Höfner "violin" bass guitar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gretsch" title="Gretsch">Gretsch Country Gentleman guitar</a>, models played by McCartney and Harrison, respectively; the <a href="/wiki/Vox_(musical_equipment)" title="Vox (musical equipment)">Vox AC30</a> amplifier behind them is the model the Beatles used during performances in the early 1960s</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although the 1965 song "Yesterday" was not the first pop record to employ orchestral strings, it marked the group's first recorded use of classical music elements. Gould observes: "The more traditional sound of strings allowed for a fresh appreciation of their talent as composers by listeners who were otherwise allergic to the din of drums and electric guitars."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007278_340-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007278-340">[333]</a></sup> They continued to experiment with string arrangements to various effect; <i>Sgt. Pepper</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s "<a href="/wiki/She%27s_Leaving_Home" title="She's Leaving Home">She's Leaving Home</a>", for instance, is "cast in the <span lang="en-US">mold</span> of a sentimental Victorian ballad", Gould writes, "its words and music filled with the clichés of musical melodrama".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007402_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007402-341">[334]</a></sup></p>
<p>The band's stylistic range expanded in another direction with their 1966 B-side "Rain", described by <a href="/wiki/Martin_C._Strong" title="Martin C. Strong">Martin Strong</a> as "the first overtly psychedelic Beatles record".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStrong2004108_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStrong2004108-342">[335]</a></sup> Other psychedelic numbers followed, such as "Tomorrow Never Knows" (recorded before "Rain"), "Strawberry Fields Forever", "<a href="/wiki/Lucy_in_the_Sky_with_Diamonds" title="Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds">Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/I_Am_the_Walrus" title="I Am the Walrus">I Am the Walrus</a>". The influence of <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a> was evident in Harrison's "<a href="/wiki/The_Inner_Light_(song)" title="The Inner Light (song)">The Inner Light</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Love_You_To" title="Love You To">Love You To</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Within_You_Without_You" title="Within You Without You">Within You Without You</a>" – Gould describes the latter two as attempts "to replicate the <a href="/wiki/Raga" title="Raga">raga</a> form in miniature".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007406.2C_462.E2.80.93463_343-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007406.2C_462.E2.80.93463-343">[336]</a></sup></p>
<p>Innovation was the most striking feature of their creative evolution, according to music historian and pianist Michael Campbell: "'A Day in the Life' encapsulates the art and achievement of the Beatles as well as any single track can. It highlights key features of their music: the sound imagination, the persistence of tuneful melody, and the close coordination between words and music. It represents a new category of song – more sophisticated than pop ... and uniquely innovative. There literally had never before been a song – classical or vernacular – that had blended so many disparate elements so imaginatively."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECampbell2008196_344-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECampbell2008196-344">[337]</a></sup> Philosophy professor Bruce Ellis Benson agrees: "the Beatles ... give us a wonderful example of how such far-ranging influences as Celtic music, rhythm and blues, and country and western could be put together in a new way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson200343_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson200343-345">[338]</a></sup></p>
<p>Author Dominic Pedler describes the way they crossed musical styles: "Far from moving sequentially from one genre to another (as is sometimes conveniently suggested) the group maintained <i>in parallel</i> their mastery of the traditional, catchy chart hit while simultaneously forging rock and dabbling with a wide range of peripheral influences from country to vaudeville. One of these threads was their take on folk music, which would form such essential groundwork for their later collisions with Indian music and philosophy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPedler2003256_346-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPedler2003256-346">[339]</a></sup> As the personal relationships between the band members grew increasingly strained, their individual tastes became more apparent. The minimalistic cover artwork for the White Album contrasted with the complexity and diversity of its music, which encompassed Lennon's "<a href="/wiki/Revolution_9" title="Revolution 9">Revolution 9</a>", whose <a href="/wiki/Musique_concr%C3%A8te" title="Musique concrète">musique concrète</a> approach was influenced by Yoko Ono; Starr's <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Pass_Me_By" title="Don't Pass Me By">Don't Pass Me By</a>"; Harrison's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_ballad" title="Rock ballad">rock ballad</a> "<a href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps" title="While My Guitar Gently Weeps">While My Guitar Gently Weeps</a>"; and the "<a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music#Origins:_late_1960s_and_early_1970s" title="Heavy metal music">proto-metal</a> roar" of McCartney's "<a href="/wiki/Helter_Skelter_(song)" title="Helter Skelter (song)">Helter Skelter</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErlewine2009d_225-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErlewine2009d-225">[219]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contribution_of_George_Martin">Contribution of George Martin</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a>'s close involvement in his role as producer made him one of the leading candidates for the informal title of the "<a href="/wiki/Fifth_Beatle" title="Fifth Beatle">fifth Beatle</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a721_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a721-347">[340]</a></sup> He applied his classical musical training in various ways, and functioned as "an informal music teacher" to the progressing songwriters, according to Gould.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007121.2C_290_348-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007121.2C_290-348">[341]</a></sup> Martin suggested to a sceptical McCartney that the arrangement of "Yesterday" should feature a string quartet accompaniment, thereby introducing the Beatles to a "hitherto unsuspected world of classical instrumental colour", in MacDonald's description.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005158_349-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005158-349">[342]</a></sup> Their creative development was also facilitated by Martin's willingness to experiment in response to their suggestions, such as adding "something <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque</a>" to a particular recording.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007290_350-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007290-350">[343]</a></sup> In addition to scoring orchestral arrangements for recordings, Martin often performed on them, playing instruments including piano, organ and <a href="/wiki/Brass_instrument" title="Brass instrument">brass</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007382.2C_405.2C_409.2C_443.2C_584_351-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007382.2C_405.2C_409.2C_443.2C_584-351">[344]</a></sup></p>
<p>Collaborating with Lennon and McCartney required Martin to adapt to their different approaches to songwriting and recording. MacDonald comments, "while [he] worked more naturally with the conventionally articulate McCartney, the challenge of catering to Lennon's intuitive approach generally spurred him to his more original arrangements, of which '<a href="/wiki/Being_for_the_Benefit_of_Mr._Kite!" title="Being for the Benefit of Mr. Kite!">Being for the Benefit of Mr. Kite!</a>' is an outstanding example."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005238_352-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005238-352">[345]</a></sup> Martin said of the two composers' distinct songwriting styles and his own stabilising influence:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Compared with Paul's songs, all of which seemed to keep in some sort of touch with reality, John's had a psychedelic, almost mystical quality ... John's imagery is one of the best things about his work – 'tangerine trees', 'marmalade skies', 'cellophane flowers' ... I always saw him as an aural <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Dal%C3%AD" title="Salvador Dalí">Salvador Dalí</a>, rather than some drug-ridden record artist. On the other hand, I would be stupid to pretend that drugs didn't figure quite heavily in the Beatles' lives at that time ... they knew that I, in my schoolmasterly role, didn't approve ... Not only was I not into it myself, I couldn't see the need for it; and there's no doubt that, if I too had been on dope, <i>Pepper</i> would never have been the album it was. Perhaps it was the combination of dope and no dope that worked, who knows?<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin1979205.E2.80.93206_353-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin1979205.E2.80.93206-353">[346]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Harrison echoed Martin's description of his stabilising role: "I think we just grew through those years together, him as the straight man and us as the loonies; but he was always there for us to interpret our madness – we used to be slightly avant-garde on certain days of the week, and he would be there as the anchor person, to communicate that through the engineers and on to the tape."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003264_354-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003264-354">[347]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_studio">In the studio</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_recording_technology" title="The Beatles' recording technology">The Beatles' recording technology</a></div>
<p>Making innovative use of technology while expanding the possibilities of recorded music, the Beatles urged experimentation by Martin and his recording engineers. Seeking ways to put chance occurrences to creative use, accidental guitar feedback, a resonating glass bottle, a tape loaded the wrong way round so that it played backwards – any of these might be incorporated into their music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHertsgaard1995103_355-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHertsgaard1995103-355">[348]</a></sup> Their desire to create new sounds on every new recording, combined with Martin's arranging abilities and the studio expertise of EMI staff engineers Norman Smith, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Townsend" title="Ken Townsend">Ken Townsend</a> and Geoff Emerick, all contributed significantly to their records from <i>Rubber Soul</i> and, especially, <i>Revolver</i> onwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHertsgaard1995103_355-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHertsgaard1995103-355">[348]</a></sup> Along with innovative studio techniques such as <a href="/wiki/Audio_signal_processing" title="Audio signal processing">sound effects</a>, unconventional microphone placements, tape loops, <a href="/wiki/Double_tracking" title="Double tracking">double tracking</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vari-speed" title="Vari-speed">vari-speed</a> recording, the Beatles augmented their songs with instruments that were unconventional in rock music at the time. These included string and brass ensembles as well as Indian instruments such as the sitar in "Norwegian Wood" and the <a href="/wiki/Swarmandal" title="Swarmandal">swarmandal</a> in "Strawberry Fields Forever".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005212_356-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005212-356">[349]</a></sup> They also used early electronic instruments such as the Mellotron, with which McCartney supplied the flute voices on the "Strawberry Fields Forever" intro,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005219_357-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005219-357">[350]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Clavioline" title="Clavioline">clavioline</a>, an electronic keyboard that created the unusual oboe-like sound on "<a href="/wiki/Baby,_You%27re_a_Rich_Man" title="Baby, You're a Rich Man">Baby, You're a Rich Man</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005259_358-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005259-358">[351]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cultural_impact_of_the_Beatles" title="Cultural impact of the Beatles">Cultural impact of the Beatles</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_on_Green_Hill_in_Almaty,_Kazakhstan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2459" data-file-width="3819" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/The_Beatles_on_Green_Hill_in_Almaty%2C_Kazakhstan.jpg/330px-The_Beatles_on_Green_Hill_in_Almaty%2C_Kazakhstan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/The_Beatles_on_Green_Hill_in_Almaty%2C_Kazakhstan.jpg/495px-The_Beatles_on_Green_Hill_in_Almaty%2C_Kazakhstan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/The_Beatles_on_Green_Hill_in_Almaty%2C_Kazakhstan.jpg/660px-The_Beatles_on_Green_Hill_in_Almaty%2C_Kazakhstan.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_on_Green_Hill_in_Almaty,_Kazakhstan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Beatles Monument in <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Former <i>Rolling Stone</i> associate editor <a href="/wiki/Robert_Greenfield" title="Robert Greenfield">Robert Greenfield</a> compared the Beatles to <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Picasso</a>, as "artists who broke through the constraints of their time period to come up with something that was unique and original ... [I]n the form of popular music, no one will ever be more revolutionary, more creative and more distinctive ..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGross2009_308-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGross2009-308">[301]</a></sup> The British poet <a href="/wiki/Philip_Larkin" title="Philip Larkin">Philip Larkin</a> described their work as "an enchanting and intoxicating hybrid of Negro rock-and-roĺl with their own adolescent romanticism", and "the first advance in popular music since the War".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-359"><a href="#cite_note-359">[352]</a></sup> They not only sparked the British Invasion of the US,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999277_360-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999277-360">[353]</a></sup> they became a globally influential phenomenon as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould20078_361-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould20078-361">[354]</a></sup> From the 1920s, the United States had dominated popular entertainment culture throughout much of the world, via <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">Hollywood</a> movies, <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, the music of Broadway and <a href="/wiki/Tin_Pan_Alley" title="Tin Pan Alley">Tin Pan Alley</a> and, later, the rock and roll that first emerged in <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis, Tennessee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould20079_293-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould20079-293">[286]</a></sup></p>
<p>Their musical innovations and commercial success inspired musicians worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould20078_361-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould20078-361">[354]</a></sup> Many artists have acknowledged the Beatles' influence and enjoyed chart success with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_artists_who_have_covered_The_Beatles" title="List of artists who have covered The Beatles">covers of their songs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_Radio_22009_362-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_Radio_22009-362">[355]</a></sup> On radio, their arrival marked the beginning of a new era; in 1968 the programme director of New York's <a href="/wiki/WABC_(AM)" title="WABC (AM)">WABC</a> radio station forbade his DJs from playing any "pre-Beatles" music, marking the defining line of what would be considered <a href="/wiki/Oldies" title="Oldies">oldies</a> on American radio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFisher2007198_363-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFisher2007198-363">[356]</a></sup> They helped to redefine the album as something more than just a few hits padded out with "<a href="/wiki/Filler_(media)" title="Filler (media)">filler</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199991_364-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199991-364">[357]</a></sup> and they were primary innovators of the modern music video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005609.E2.80.93610_365-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005609.E2.80.93610-365">[358]</a></sup> The Shea Stadium show with which they opened their <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_1965_US_tour" title="The Beatles' 1965 US tour">1965 North American tour</a> attracted an estimated 55,600 people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992181_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992181-127">[122]</a></sup> then the largest audience in concert history; Spitz describes the event as a "major breakthrough ... a giant step toward reshaping the concert business".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005576.E2.80.93578_366-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005576.E2.80.93578-366">[359]</a></sup> Emulation of their clothing and especially their hairstyles, which became a mark of rebellion, had a global impact on fashion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007345_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007345-102">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Gould, the Beatles changed the way people listened to popular music and experienced its role in their lives. From what began as the Beatlemania fad, the group's popularity grew into what was seen as an embodiment of sociocultural movements of the decade. As icons of the <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">1960s counterculture</a>, Gould continues, they became a catalyst for <a href="/wiki/Bohemianism" title="Bohemianism">bohemianism</a> and activism in various social and political arenas, fuelling movements such as <a href="/wiki/Feminist_movement" title="Feminist movement">women's liberation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gay_liberation" title="Gay liberation">gay liberation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_movement" title="Environmental movement">environmentalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould20078.E2.80.939_367-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould20078.E2.80.939-367">[360]</a></sup> According to Peter Lavezzoli, after the "more popular than Jesus" controversy in 1966, the Beatles felt considerable pressure to say the right things and "began a concerted effort to spread a message of wisdom and higher consciousness".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176-152">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_achievements">Awards and achievements</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_the_Beatles" title="List of awards and nominations received by the Beatles">List of awards and nominations received by the Beatles</a></div>
<p>In 1965, Queen Elizabeth II appointed Lennon, McCartney, Harrison and Starr <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Members of the Order of the British Empire (MBE)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005556_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005556-119">[114]</a></sup> The film <i>Let It Be</i> (1970) won the 1971 Academy Award for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Music_(Scoring)#1970s" title="Academy Award for Best Music (Scoring)">Best Original Song Score</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200696_258-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200696-258">[252]</a></sup> The recipients of seven Grammy Awards<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrammy.com_368-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrammy.com-368">[361]</a></sup> and fifteen <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Awards" title="Ivor Novello Awards">Ivor Novello Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a559.E2.80.93560_369-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a559.E2.80.93560-369">[362]</a></sup> the Beatles have been awarded six <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">Diamond albums</a>, as well as 24 <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">Multi-Platinum albums</a>, 39 <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">Platinum albums</a> and 45 <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">Gold albums</a> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERIAA2009b_268-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERIAA2009b-268">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERIAA2009c_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERIAA2009c-370">[363]</a></sup> In the UK, the Beatles have four <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">Multi-Platinum albums</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">Platinum albums</a>, eight <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">Gold albums</a> and one <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">Silver album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBritish_Phonographic_Industry2009_269-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBritish_Phonographic_Industry2009-269">[263]</a></sup> They were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1988.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling band</a> in history, estimates of the Beatles sales range from one billion discs and tapes as of 1982<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guinness_371-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guinness-371">[364]</a></sup> to 600 million records, tapes and CDs as of 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ApplePR_372-0"><a href="#cite_note-ApplePR-372">[365]</a></sup> They have had more number-one albums on the British charts, fifteen,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlennie2012_373-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlennie2012-373">[366]</a></sup> and sold more singles in the UK, 21.9 million, than any other act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOfficial_Chart_Company2012_374-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOfficial_Chart_Company2012-374">[367]</a></sup> In 2004, <i>Rolling Stone</i> ranked the Beatles as the best artist of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECostello2004_375-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECostello2004-375">[368]</a></sup> They ranked number one on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> magazine's list of the all-time most successful Hot 100 artists, released in 2008 to celebrate the US singles chart's 50th anniversary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBillboard2008a_376-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBillboard2008a-376">[369]</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Beatles&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, they hold the record for most number-one hits on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, with twenty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hot100_377-0"><a href="#cite_note-hot100-377">[370]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> certifies that the Beatles have sold 178 million units in the US, more than any other artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERIAA2009a_378-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERIAA2009a-378">[371]</a></sup> They were collectively included in <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine's compilation of <a href="/wiki/Time_100:_The_Most_Important_People_of_the_Century" title="Time 100: The Most Important People of the Century">the twentieth century's 100 most influential people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoder1998_379-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoder1998-379">[372]</a></sup> In 2014, they received the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-380"><a href="#cite_note-380">[373]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Song_catalogue">Song catalogue</span></h2>
<p>Through 1969, the Beatles' catalogue was published almost exclusively by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Songs" title="Northern Songs">Northern Songs Ltd.</a>, a company formed in February 1963 by music publisher <a href="/wiki/Dick_James" title="Dick James">Dick James</a> specifically for Lennon and McCartney, though it later acquired songs by other artists. The company was organised with James and his partner, Emmanuel Silver, owning a controlling interest, variously described as 51% or 50% plus one share. McCartney had 20%. Reports again vary concerning Lennon's portion – 19 or 20% – and Brian Epstein's – 9 or 10% – which he received in lieu of a 25% band management fee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200615.E2.80.9317_381-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200615.E2.80.9317-381">[374]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman1996169.E2.80.9371.2C_368.E2.80.93369_382-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman1996169.E2.80.9371.2C_368.E2.80.93369-382">[375]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002178_383-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002178-383">[376]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1965, the company went public. Five million shares were created, of which the original principals retained 3.75 million. James and Silver each received 937,500 shares (18.75% of 5 million); Lennon and McCartney each received 750,000 shares (15%); and Epstein's management company, NEMS Enterprises, received 375,000 shares (7.5%). Of the 1.25 million shares put up for sale, Harrison and Starr each acquired 40,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200637.E2.80.9338_384-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200637.E2.80.9338-384">[377]</a></sup> At the time of the stock offering, Lennon and McCartney renewed their three-year publishing contracts, binding them to Northern Songs until 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200642_385-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200642-385">[378]</a></sup></p>
<p>Harrison created <a href="/wiki/Harrisongs" title="Harrisongs">Harrisongs</a> to represent his Beatles compositions, but signed a three-year contract with Northern Songs that gave it the copyright to his work through March 1968, which included "<a href="/wiki/Taxman" title="Taxman">Taxman</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Within_You_Without_You" title="Within You Without You">Within You Without You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200645_386-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200645-386">[379]</a></sup> The songs on which Starr received co-writing credit before 1968, such as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/What_Goes_On_(The_Beatles_song)" title="What Goes On (The Beatles song)">What Goes On</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flying_(The_Beatles_song)" title="Flying (The Beatles song)">Flying</a>", were also Northern Songs copyrights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200646.E2.80.9347_387-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200646.E2.80.9347-387">[380]</a></sup> Harrison did not renew his contract with Northern Songs when it ended, signing instead with <a href="/wiki/Apple_Corps" title="Apple Corps">Apple Publishing</a> while retaining the copyright to his work from that point on. Harrisongs thus owns the rights to his later Beatles songs such as "<a href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps" title="While My Guitar Gently Weeps">While My Guitar Gently Weeps</a>" and "Something". That year, as well, Starr created <a href="/wiki/Startling_Music" title="Startling Music">Startling Music</a>, which holds the rights to his Beatles compositions, "Don't Pass Me By" and "<a href="/wiki/Octopus%27s_Garden" title="Octopus's Garden">Octopus's Garden</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200660.E2.80.9361_388-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200660.E2.80.9361-388">[381]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005351_389-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005351-389">[382]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1969, James arranged to sell his and his partner's shares of Northern Songs to the British broadcasting company <a href="/wiki/Associated_Television" title="Associated Television">Associated Television</a> (ATV), founded by impresario <a href="/wiki/Lew_Grade" title="Lew Grade">Lew Grade</a>, without first informing the Beatles. The band then made a bid to gain controlling interest by attempting to work out a deal with a consortium of London brokerage firms that had accumulated a 14% holding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman1996369.E2.80.93372_390-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman1996369.E2.80.93372-390">[383]</a></sup> The deal collapsed over the objections of Lennon, who declared, "I'm sick of being fucked about by men in suits sitting on their fat arses in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman1996372_391-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman1996372-391">[384]</a></sup> By the end of May, ATV had acquired a majority stake in Northern Songs, controlling nearly the entire Lennon–McCartney catalogue, as well as any future material until 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1998296_392-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1998296-392">[385]</a></sup> In frustration, Lennon and McCartney sold their shares to ATV in late October 1969.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999236_393-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999236-393">[386]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1981, financial losses by ATV's parent company, ACC, led it to attempt to sell its music division. According to authors Brian Southall and Rupert Perry, Grade contacted McCartney, offering ATV Music and Northern Songs for $30 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006129_394-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006129-394">[387]</a></sup> According to an account McCartney gave in 1995, he met with Grade and explained he was interested solely in the Northern Songs catalogue, if Grade were ever willing to "separate off" that portion of ATV Music. Soon afterwards, Grade offered to sell him Northern Songs for £20 million, giving the ex-Beatle "a week or so" to decide. By McCartney's account, he and Ono countered with a £5 million bid that was rejected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006130_395-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006130-395">[388]</a></sup> According to reports at the time, Grade refused to separate Northern Songs, and turned down an offer of £21–25 million from McCartney and Ono for ATV Music. In 1982, ACC as a whole was sold to Australian business magnate <a href="/wiki/Robert_Holmes_%C3%A0_Court" title="Robert Holmes à Court">Robert Holmes à Court</a> for £60 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006130.2C_139_396-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006130.2C_139-396">[389]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three years later, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> purchased ATV for a reported $47.5 million. The acquisition gave him control over the publishing rights to more than 200 Beatles songs, as well as 40,000 other copyrights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006140.2C_174.2C_176_397-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006140.2C_174.2C_176-397">[390]</a></sup> In 1995, in a deal that earned him a reported $110 million, Jackson merged his music publishing business with <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>, creating a new company, <a href="/wiki/Sony/ATV_Music_Publishing" title="Sony/ATV Music Publishing">Sony/ATV Music Publishing</a>, in which he held a 50% stake. The merger made the new company, then valued at over half a billion dollars, the third largest music publisher in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006198_398-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006198-398">[391]</a></sup> In 2016, Sony acquired Jackson's share of Sony/ATV from the Jackson estate for $750 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-399"><a href="#cite_note-399">[392]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the lack of publishing rights to most of their songs, Lennon's estate and McCartney continue to receive their respective shares of the writers' royalties, which together are 33⅓% of total commercial proceeds in the US and which vary elsewhere around the world between 50 and 55%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006195_400-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006195-400">[393]</a></sup> Two of Lennon and McCartney's earliest songs – "Love Me Do" and "P.S. I Love You" – were published by an EMI subsidiary, Ardmore &amp; Beechwood, before they signed with James. McCartney acquired their publishing rights from Ardmore in the mid-1980s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006192.E2.80.93193_401-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006192.E2.80.93193-401">[394]</a></sup> and they are the only two Beatles songs owned by McCartney's company MPL Communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002536_402-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002536-402">[395]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vee-Jay company president <a href="/wiki/Ewart_Abner" title="Ewart Abner">Ewart Abner</a> resigned after it was disclosed he used company funds to cover gambling debts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpizer200436_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpizer200436-77">[77]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Harrison's ringing 12-string inspired <a href="/wiki/Roger_McGuinn" title="Roger McGuinn">Roger McGuinn</a>, who obtained his own Rickenbacker and used it to craft the trademark sound of <a href="/wiki/The_Byrds" title="The Byrds">the Byrds</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007286.E2.80.93287_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007286.E2.80.93287-96">[95]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-100">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the same week in April 1964, a third American Beatles LP joined the two already in circulation; two of the three reached the first spot on the <i>Billboard</i> albums chart, the third peaked at number two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992351_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992351-99">[97]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Starr was briefly hospitalised after a <a href="/wiki/Tonsillectomy" title="Tonsillectomy">tonsillectomy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Nicol" title="Jimmie Nicol">Jimmie Nicol</a> sat in on drums for the first five dates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992160.E2.80.93161.2C_163_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992160.E2.80.93161.2C_163-104">[101]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In September, the Beatles refused to play a show in Florida until the local promoter assured them that the audience would not be <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States" title="Racial segregation in the United States">racially segregated</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992171_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992171-110">[106]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-197"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-197">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It was speculated that he was concerned that the band might not renew his management contract, due to expire in October, over discontent with his supervision of business matters, particularly regarding <a href="/wiki/Seltaeb" title="Seltaeb">Seltaeb</a>, the company that handled their US merchandising rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002227.E2.80.93228_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002227.E2.80.93228-196">[191]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-273"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-273">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The band unsuccessfully attempted to block the 1977 release of <i><a href="/wiki/Live!_at_the_Star-Club_in_Hamburg,_Germany;_1962" title="Live! at the Star-Club in Hamburg, Germany; 1962">Live! at the Star-Club in Hamburg, Germany; 1962</a></i>. The independently issued album compiled recordings made during the group's <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_Hamburg" title="The Beatles in Hamburg">Hamburg residency</a>, taped on a basic recording machine using only one microphone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a124.E2.80.93126_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a124.E2.80.93126-272">[266]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

The London-based company has administered the catalogue of The Beatles releases of the 1960s that have sold to date more than 600 million records, tapes and CDs.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Beatles&amp;rft.atitle=Cirque+du+Soleil%2C+Apple+Corps+Ltd.+and+The+Mirage+Partner+to+Create+an+Unprecedented+Live+Theatre+Production&amp;rft.date=2004-10-14&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.prnewswire.com%2Fnews-releases%2Fcirque-du-soleil-apple-corps-ltd-and-the-mirage-partner-to-create-an-unprecedented-live-theatre-production-74300072.html&amp;rft.jtitle=prnewswire.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
